| **\<a name="pumpTesting"\>\</a\>Packer testing, pump testing, slug testing**\<br /\> | N/A | N/A | Packer tests consist of isolating specific sections (usually 10 ft) of a bedrock \<span id="<a href="GRmark_c68c03980d8a732b1e67a543061c47a1c96b23c1_borehole" class="wikilink">GRmark_c68c03980d8a732b1e67a543061c47a1c96b23c1_borehole</a>:0"\>\<span id="<a href="GRmark_c68c03980d8a732b1e67a543061c47a1c96b23c1_borehole" class="wikilink">GRmark_c68c03980d8a732b1e67a543061c47a1c96b23c1_borehole</a>:0"\>\<span id="<a href="GRmark_c68c03980d8a732b1e67a543061c47a1c96b23c1_borehole" class="wikilink">GRmark_c68c03980d8a732b1e67a543061c47a1c96b23c1_borehole</a>:0"\>borehole\</span\>\</span\>\</span\> with inflatable packers (bladders) so that water-quality samples can be collected and aquifer tests can be conducted.\<br /\>An aquifer test (or a pumping test) is conducted to evaluate an aquifer by "stimulating" the aquifer through constant pumping, and observing the aquifer's "response" (drawdown) in observation wells.\<br /\>A slug test is a particular type of aquifer test where water is quickly added or removed from a groundwater well, and the change in hydraulic head is monitored through time, to determine the near-well aquifer characteristics. |

| \<a name="hydrogeologicalFramework"\>\</a\>**Hydrogeological Framework** | N/A | N/A | A collection of \<span id="<a href="GRmark_5a773fdfbb7e0b391815c4a577be41dbf29bd12b_hydrogeological" class="wikilink">GRmark_5a773fdfbb7e0b391815c4a577be41dbf29bd12b_hydrogeological</a>:0"\>\<span id="<a href="GRmark_5a773fdfbb7e0b391815c4a577be41dbf29bd12b_hydrogeological" class="wikilink">GRmark_5a773fdfbb7e0b391815c4a577be41dbf29bd12b_hydrogeological</a>:0"\>\<span id="<a href="GRmark_5a773fdfbb7e0b391815c4a577be41dbf29bd12b_hydrogeological" class="wikilink">GRmark_5a773fdfbb7e0b391815c4a577be41dbf29bd12b_hydrogeological</a>:0"\>\<span id="<a href="GRmark_5a773fdfbb7e0b391815c4a577be41dbf29bd12b_hydrogeological" class="wikilink">GRmark_5a773fdfbb7e0b391815c4a577be41dbf29bd12b_hydrogeological</a>:0"\>hydrogeological\</span\>\</span\>\</span\>\</span\> units which forms a \<span id="<a href="GRmark_5a773fdfbb7e0b391815c4a577be41dbf29bd12b_hydrogeological" class="wikilink">GRmark_5a773fdfbb7e0b391815c4a577be41dbf29bd12b_hydrogeological</a>:1"\>\<span id="<a href="GRmark_5a773fdfbb7e0b391815c4a577be41dbf29bd12b_hydrogeological" class="wikilink">GRmark_5a773fdfbb7e0b391815c4a577be41dbf29bd12b_hydrogeological</a>:1"\>\<span id="<a href="GRmark_5a773fdfbb7e0b391815c4a577be41dbf29bd12b_hydrogeological" class="wikilink">GRmark_5a773fdfbb7e0b391815c4a577be41dbf29bd12b_hydrogeological</a>:1"\>\<span id="<a href="GRmark_5a773fdfbb7e0b391815c4a577be41dbf29bd12b_hydrogeological" class="wikilink">GRmark_5a773fdfbb7e0b391815c4a577be41dbf29bd12b_hydrogeological</a>:1"\>hydrogeological\</span\>\</span\>\</span\>\</span\> context. |
|  | \<span id="<a href="GRmark_b6ce475d26f7ec4fa466cc0ebb240b9b4a2ec290_hguID" class="wikilink">GRmark_b6ce475d26f7ec4fa466cc0ebb240b9b4a2ec290_hguID</a>:0"\>\<span id="<a href="GRmark_b6ce475d26f7ec4fa466cc0ebb240b9b4a2ec290_hguID" class="wikilink">GRmark_b6ce475d26f7ec4fa466cc0ebb240b9b4a2ec290_hguID</a>:0"\>\<span id="<a href="GRmark_b6ce475d26f7ec4fa466cc0ebb240b9b4a2ec290_hguID" class="wikilink">GRmark_b6ce475d26f7ec4fa466cc0ebb240b9b4a2ec290_hguID</a>:0"\>\<span id="<a href="GRmark_b6ce475d26f7ec4fa466cc0ebb240b9b4a2ec290_hguID" class="wikilink">GRmark_b6ce475d26f7ec4fa466cc0ebb240b9b4a2ec290_hguID</a>:0"\>hguID\</span\>\</span\>\</span\>\</span\> | URI | Identification of the \<span id="<a href="GRmark_3b7c2d0218267fffa47f4222dff6d6a4a547ea77_hydrogeological" class="wikilink">GRmark_3b7c2d0218267fffa47f4222dff6d6a4a547ea77_hydrogeological</a>:0"\>\<span id="<a href="GRmark_3b7c2d0218267fffa47f4222dff6d6a4a547ea77_hydrogeological" class="wikilink">GRmark_3b7c2d0218267fffa47f4222dff6d6a4a547ea77_hydrogeological</a>:0"\>\<span id="<a href="GRmark_3b7c2d0218267fffa47f4222dff6d6a4a547ea77_hydrogeological" class="wikilink">GRmark_3b7c2d0218267fffa47f4222dff6d6a4a547ea77_hydrogeological</a>:0"\>\<span id="<a href="GRmark_3b7c2d0218267fffa47f4222dff6d6a4a547ea77_hydrogeological" class="wikilink">GRmark_3b7c2d0218267fffa47f4222dff6d6a4a547ea77_hydrogeological</a>:0"\>hydrogeological\</span\>\</span\>\</span\>\</span\> units |

| \<a name="piezometricSurface"\>\</a\>**Piezometric Surface** | N/A | N/A | A surface that represents the level to which water will rise in tightly cased wells. If the head varies significantly with depth in the aquifer, then there may be more than one \<span id="<a href="GRmark_ab4c3b99c9fb8c7b7ed275991494af8ad8c5f281_potentiometric" class="wikilink">GRmark_ab4c3b99c9fb8c7b7ed275991494af8ad8c5f281_potentiometric</a>:0"\>\<span id="<a href="GRmark_ab4c3b99c9fb8c7b7ed275991494af8ad8c5f281_potentiometric" class="wikilink">GRmark_ab4c3b99c9fb8c7b7ed275991494af8ad8c5f281_potentiometric</a>:0"\>\<span id="<a href="GRmark_ab4c3b99c9fb8c7b7ed275991494af8ad8c5f281_potentiometric" class="wikilink">GRmark_ab4c3b99c9fb8c7b7ed275991494af8ad8c5f281_potentiometric</a>:0"\>\<span id="<a href="GRmark_ab4c3b99c9fb8c7b7ed275991494af8ad8c5f281_potentiometric" class="wikilink">GRmark_ab4c3b99c9fb8c7b7ed275991494af8ad8c5f281_potentiometric</a>:0"\>potentiometric\</span\>\</span\>\</span\>\</span\> surface. The water table is a particular \<span id="<a href="GRmark_081248ffe70920354a75e11178a73205d582edd3_potentiometric" class="wikilink">GRmark_081248ffe70920354a75e11178a73205d582edd3_potentiometric</a>:0"\>\<span id="<a href="GRmark_081248ffe70920354a75e11178a73205d582edd3_potentiometric" class="wikilink">GRmark_081248ffe70920354a75e11178a73205d582edd3_potentiometric</a>:0"\>\<span id="<a href="GRmark_081248ffe70920354a75e11178a73205d582edd3_potentiometric" class="wikilink">GRmark_081248ffe70920354a75e11178a73205d582edd3_potentiometric</a>:0"\>\<span id="<a href="GRmark_081248ffe70920354a75e11178a73205d582edd3_potentiometric" class="wikilink">GRmark_081248ffe70920354a75e11178a73205d582edd3_potentiometric</a>:0"\>potentiometric\</span\>\</span\>\</span\>\</span\> surface for an unconfined aquifer. |

-- [Main\<span id="GRmark_5545b17da23716ee2b839f5e54f1c6687a91f50f\_.:0"\>\<span id="GRmark_5545b17da23716ee2b839f5e54f1c6687a91f50f\_.:0"\>\<span id="GRmark_5545b17da23716ee2b839f5e54f1c6687a91f50f\_.:0"\>\<span id="GRmark_5545b17da23716ee2b839f5e54f1c6687a91f50f\_.:0"\>.\</span\>\</span\>\</span\>\</span\>FrancoisLetourneau](Main.FrancoisLetourneau) - 14 \<span id="<a href="GRmark_5545b17da23716ee2b839f5e54f1c6687a91f50f_dec" class="wikilink">GRmark_5545b17da23716ee2b839f5e54f1c6687a91f50f_dec</a>:1"\>\<span id="<a href="GRmark_5545b17da23716ee2b839f5e54f1c6687a91f50f_dec" class="wikilink">GRmark_5545b17da23716ee2b839f5e54f1c6687a91f50f_dec</a>:1"\>\<span id="<a href="GRmark_5545b17da23716ee2b839f5e54f1c6687a91f50f_dec" class="wikilink">GRmark_5545b17da23716ee2b839f5e54f1c6687a91f50f_dec</a>:1"\>\<span id="<a href="GRmark_5545b17da23716ee2b839f5e54f1c6687a91f50f_dec" class="wikilink">GRmark_5545b17da23716ee2b839f5e54f1c6687a91f50f_dec</a>:1"\>dec\</span\>\</span\>\</span\>\</span\> 2012

**Features from INSPIRE <a href="HydrogeologyCore" class="wikilink">HydrogeologyCore</a> model, draft version 2.9.9**(With small corrections):

\<table align="left" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="1"\> \<tbody\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\<a name="<a href="I_ActiveWell" class="wikilink">I_ActiveWell</a>"\>\</a\>**<a href="ActiveWell" class="wikilink">ActiveWell</a>\<br /\>**(subtype of [Well](#I_Well))\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

N/A\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

N/A\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

A well influencing the groundwater resources (or state)of the groundwater body within the aquifer.\<br /\>Description: The most common examples of Active Well are: extracting, artificial recharging, or dewatering wells.\<br /\>Note: <a href="ActiveWell" class="wikilink">ActiveWell</a> by extracting, recharging or dewatering influences and changes the state of groundwater body.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

activityType\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

<a href="WellActivityType" class="wikilink">WellActivityType</a> \<br /\>(<a href="CodeList" class="wikilink">CodeList</a>)\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

The type of activity carried out by the well.\<br /\>Description: Indicates if the well is used for extracting, recharging, dewatering etc of the groundwater resources.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

**\<a name="<a href="I_Aquiclude" class="wikilink">I_Aquiclude</a>"\>\</a\>Aquiclude**\<br /\>(subtype of [HydrogeologicalUnit](#I_HydrogeologicalUnit)) \</td\> \<td width="56"\>

N/A\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

N/A\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

An impermeable body of rock or stratum of sediment that acts as a barrier to the flow of groundwater.\<br /\>Description: A formation which, although porous and capable of absorbing water slowly, will not transmit water fast enough to furnish an appreciable supply for a well or spring. Aquicludes are characterized by very low values of "leakage" (the ratio of vertical \_Hydraulic\_ *Conductivity*to thickness), so that they transmit only minor inter-aquifer flow and also have very low rates of yield from compressible storage. Therefore, they constitute boundaries of aquifer flow systems.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\<a name="<a href="I_Aquifer" class="wikilink">I_Aquifer</a>"\>\</a\>**Aquifer\<br /\>**(subtype of [HydrogeologicalUnit](#I_HydrogeologicalUnit))\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

N/A\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

N/A\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

A wet underground layer of water-bearing permeable rock or unconsolidated materials (gravel, sand, silt, or clay) from which groundwater can be usefully extracted using a water well. It can be zone of fractures related to Geologic Structure  a part of geological formation.\<br /\>Description: An underground geological formation able to store and yield water. Groundwater body flows through aquifers.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

\*aquiferType\*\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

<a href="AquiferType" class="wikilink">AquiferType</a> \<br /\>(enumeration)\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

The type of aquifer.\<br /\>Description: Water in an Aquifer is, or is not, under pressure. Based on that unconfined, confined, artesian, or subartesian types are distinguished.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

\*mediaType\*\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

<a href="AquiferMediaType" class="wikilink">AquiferMediaType</a> \<br /\>(enumeration)\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

The classification of the medium in which the groundwater flow occurs.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

\*isExploited\*\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

Boolean\<br /\>(voidable)\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

Indicates if groundwater from aquifer is exploited by wells or intakes\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\> \</td\> \<td width="56"\>

\*isMainInSystem\*\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

Boolean\<br /\>(voidable)\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

Indicates if aquifer is the main useful aquifer in the aquifer system\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

\*vulnerabilityToPollution\*\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

<a href="QuantityValue" class="wikilink">QuantityValue</a> \<br /\>(voidable)\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

DRASTIC index value or interval of values determining the potential degree of aquifer risk arising from the geological structure, hydrogeological conditions and the existence of real or potential source of contamination.\<br /\>Description: A single value should be used if it is determined directly from the DRASTIC method. If attribute data comes from another data source which is expressed by categorized items, for example: low, moderate or high, interval should be used expressed by lowest and highest value of category. EXAMPLE: Moderate means interval from 101 to 140.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

\*permeabilityCoefficient\*\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

<a href="QuantityValue" class="wikilink">QuantityValue</a> \<br /\>(voidable)\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

The volume of an incompressible fluid that will flow in unit time through a unit cube of a porous substance across which a unit pressure difference is maintained.\<br /\>Description: The parameter represents the hydraulic conductivity of a rock container. Describes the ease with which water can move through pore spaces or fractures. It depends on the intrinsic permeability of the material and on the degree of saturation.\<br /\>Note: Because of their high porosity and permeability, sand and gravel have higher hydraulic conductivity than clay or unfractured granite aquifers.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

\*storativityCoefficient\*\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

<a href="QuantityValue" class="wikilink">QuantityValue</a> \<br /\>(voidable)\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

The ability of an aquifer to store water.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

\*hydroGeochemicalRockType\*\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

<a href="HydroGeochemicalRockTerm" class="wikilink">HydroGeochemicalRockTerm</a> \<br /\>(<a href="CodeList" class="wikilink">CodeList</a>, voidable)\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

The rock type with respect to the soluble rock components and their hydrogeochemical influence of groundwater.\<br /\>Description: Defines the prevailing geochemical character of natural groundwater within the Aquifer.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\<a name="<a href="I_AquiferSystem" class="wikilink">I_AquiferSystem</a>"\>\</a\>**<a href="AquiferSystem" class="wikilink">AquiferSystem</a>**\<br /\>(subtype of [HydrogeologicalUnit](#I_HydrogeologicalUnit))\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

N/A\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

N/A\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

A collection of aquifers and aquitards, which together constitute the environment of groundwater - "communicating vessels", that are filled or can be filled with water.\<br /\>Description: Attributes of Aquifer System and its components determine the feasibility of water collection, its movement, as well as the impact on its chemical state.\<br /\>Note: The Aquifer System components and their attributes (including geometry) are relatively stable over time except in special cases.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

\*isLayered\*\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

Boolean\<br /\>(voidable)\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

Indicates if the <a href="AquiferSystem" class="wikilink">AquiferSystem</a> consists of more than one layer.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

**\<a name="<a href="I_Aquitard" class="wikilink">I_Aquitard</a>"\>\</a\>Aquitard\<br /\>**(subtype of [HydrogeologicalUnit](#I_HydrogeologicalUnit))\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

N/A\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

N/A\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

A saturated, but poorly permeable bed that impedes ground-water movement.\<br /\>Description: It does not yield water freely to wells, but may transmit appreciable water to or from adjacent aquifers and, where sufficiently thick, may constitute an important ground-water storage unit. Aquitards are characterized by values of leakance that may range from relatively low to relatively high. A really extensive aquitard of relatively low leakance may function regionally as boundaries of aquifer flow systems.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

\*approximatePermeabilityCoefficient\*\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

<a href="QuantityValue" class="wikilink">QuantityValue</a> \<br /\>(voidable)\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

The parameter represents the hydraulic conductivity of a poorly permeable rock or other formation. In that case, a value of permeability is most often approximate.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

\*approximateStorativityCoefficient\*\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

<a href="QuantityValue" class="wikilink">QuantityValue</a> \<br /\>(voidable)\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

The ability of an aquitard to store water.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

**\<a name="<a href="I_GroundwaterBody" class="wikilink">I_GroundwaterBody</a>"\>\</a\><a href="GroundwaterBody" class="wikilink">GroundwaterBody</a>**\<br /\> \</td\> \<td width="56"\>

N/A\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

N/A\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

A distinct volume of groundwater within an aquifer or system of aquifers, which is hydraulically separated from nearby groundwater bodies.\<br /\>Description: Groundwater bodies form the principal management units under the European Water Framework Directive (2000/60/CE, 2000). They should be hydraulically continuous entities, and must be defined on the basis of flow or abstraction, and are inextricably linked to surface water bodies.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\> \</td\> \<td width="56"\>

\*Id\*\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

Identifier\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

External object identifier of the spatial feature.\<br /\>Note: An external object identifier is a unique object identifier published by the responsible body, which may be used by external applications to reference the spatial feature. The identifier is an identifier of the spatial feature, not an identifier of the real-world phenomenon.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

\*approximateHorizontalExtend\*\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

<a href="GM_Surface" class="wikilink">GM_Surface</a>\<br /\>(voidable)\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

The geometry defining the approximate boundary of the <a href="GroundWaterBody" class="wikilink">GroundWaterBody</a>.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

\*conditionOfGroundWaterBody\*\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

<a href="ConditionOfGroundwater" class="wikilink">ConditionOfGroundwater</a> \<br /\>(enumeration)\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

The approximate degree of change to groundwater as a result of human activity.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

\*mineralization\*\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

<a href="WaterTypeValue" class="wikilink">WaterTypeValue</a> \<br /\>(voidable)\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

One of the main chemical characteristics of water. A value is a sum of all water chemical concentration components.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

\*piezometricState\*\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

<a href="PiezometricState" class="wikilink">PiezometricState</a> \<br /\>(voidable, dataType)\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

Specifies the piezometric state of the <a href="GroundwaterBody" class="wikilink">GroundwaterBody</a>.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

\*beginLifespanVersion\*\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

<a href="DateTime" class="wikilink">DateTime</a> \<br /\>(lifeCycleInfo, voidable)\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

Date and time at which this version of the spatial object was inserted or changed in the spatial data set.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

\*endLifespanVersion\*\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

<a href="DateTime" class="wikilink">DateTime</a> \<br /\>(lifeCycleInfo, voidable)\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

\<a name="<a href="I_HydrogeologicalObject" class="wikilink">I_HydrogeologicalObject</a>"\>\</a\>**<a href="HydrogeologicalObject" class="wikilink">HydrogeologicalObject</a>\<br /\>**(Abstract)

\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

N/A\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

N/A\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

An abstract class for man-made facilities or natural features that have an interaction with the hydrogeological system.\<br /\>Description: Hydrogeological objects may be natural (eg. spring) or the manmade (eg. wells). The vast majority of hydrogeological objects are manmade. Dynamic object can change state of groundwater body and as consequence state of flow system.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

\*Id\*\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

Identifier\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

External object identifier of the spatial feature.\<br /\>Note: An external object identifier is a unique object identifier published by the responsible body, which may be used by external applications to reference the spatial feature. The identifier is an identifier of the spatial feature, not an identifier of the real-world phenomenon.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

\*geometry\*\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

<a href="GM_Primitive" class="wikilink">GM_Primitive</a>\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

The geometry defining the spatial location of the <a href="HydrogeologicalObject" class="wikilink">HydrogeologicalObject</a>.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

<a href="PT_FreeText" class="wikilink">PT_FreeText</a>\<br /\>(voidable)\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

The name or code of the <a href="HydrogeologicalObject" class="wikilink">HydrogeologicalObject</a>.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

<a href="PT_FreeText" class="wikilink">PT_FreeText</a>\<br /\>(voidable)\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

The description of the <a href="HydrogeologicalObject" class="wikilink">HydrogeologicalObject</a>.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

\*beginLifespanVersion\*\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

<a href="DateTime" class="wikilink">DateTime</a> \<br /\>(lifeCycleInfo, voidable)\</td\> \<td width="518"\>

Date and time at which this version of the spatial object was inserted or changed in the spatial data set.\</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

**<a href="HG_FeatureOccurrence" class="wikilink">HG_FeatureOccurrence</a>** \</td\> \<td width="56"\>

N/A \</td\> \<td width="188"\>

N/A \</td\> \<td width="518"\>

-- Definition --\<br /\><a href="HydrogeologicalFeatureAppearence" class="wikilink">HydrogeologicalFeatureAppearence</a> class is a geometric representation of <a href="HydrogeologicalFeature" class="wikilink">HydrogeologicalFeature</a> calaas. <a href="HydrogeologicalFeature" class="wikilink">HydrogeologicalFeature</a> instance (object) could be represented by many various instances of <a href="HydrogeologicalFeatureAppearence" class="wikilink">HydrogeologicalFeatureAppearence</a> class.\<br /\>-- Note --\<br /\>Class equivalent to <a href="HydrogeologicMappedFeature" class="wikilink">HydrogeologicMappedFeature</a> in GWML model and <a href="GeologicMappedFeature" class="wikilink">GeologicMappedFeature</a> in <a href="GeoSciML" class="wikilink">GeoSciML</a>:\<br /\>"Mapped feature more oriented on spatial temporal (although geometries could handle this).\<br /\>A physical hydrogeologic feature represented on a map."\<br /\>Here, meaning of this class is wider then in GWML and similar to <a href="MappedFeature" class="wikilink">MappedFeature</a> class in <a href="GeoSciML" class="wikilink">GeoSciML</a>:\<br /\>A <a href="MappedFeature" class="wikilink">MappedFeature</a> is part of a geological interpretation.\<br /\>It provides a link between a notional feature (description package) and one spatial representation of it, or part of it. (Exposures, Surface Traces and Intercepts, etc)\<br /\> \* the specific bounded occurrence, such as an outcrop or map polygon\<br /\> \* the Mapped Feature carries a geometry or shape\<br /\> o the association with a Geologic Feature (legend item) provides specification of all the other descriptors\<br /\> o the association with a Sampling Feature provides the context and dimensionality \<br /\>A Mapped Feature is always associated with some sampling feature - e.g. a mapping surface, a section, a Borehole (see <a href="BoreHolesAndObservation" class="wikilink">BoreHolesAndObservation</a>) etc. As noted on the diagram, if the associated sampling feature is a Borehole, then the shape associated with the <a href="MappedFeature" class="wikilink">MappedFeature</a> will usually be either a point or an interval. This reconciles the 2-D ("map", section) and 1-D (borehole, traverse) viewpoints in a common abstraction." \</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

**<a href="HG_ConeOfDepression" class="wikilink">HG_ConeOfDepression</a>\<br /\>**(subtype of <a href="HydrogeologicalZone" class="wikilink">HydrogeologicalZone</a>) \</td\> \<td width="56"\> N/A\</td\> \<td width="188"\>

N/A \</td\> \<td width="518"\>

-- Definition --\<br /\>(from GWML) A cone of depression occurs in an aquifer when ground water is pumped from a well. In an unconfined (water table) aquifer, this is an actual depression of the water levels. In confined (artesian) aquifers, the cone of depression is a reduction in the pressure head surrounding the pumped well (please see earlier articles for discussion of head).\<br /\><http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cone_of_depression> \<br /\>A depression in the groundwater table or potentiometric surface that has the shape of an inverted cone and develops around a well from which water is being withdrawn. Its trace (perimeter) on the land surface defines the zone of influence of a well. Also called pumping cone and cone of drawdown. (<http://www.wrds.uwyo.edu/wrds/deq/whp/whpgloss.html>)\<br /\>he zone around a well in an unconfined aquifer that is normally saturated, but becomes unsaturated as a well is pumped, leaving an area where the water table dips down to form a cone shape. The shape of the cone is influenced by porosity and the water yield or pumping rate of the well. The land surface overlying the cone of depression is referred to as the area of influence.\<br /\><http://www.groundwater.org/gi/gwglossary.html#C> \</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\</td\> \<td width="56"\> **centeredAt** \</td\> \<td width="188"\>

<a href="GM_Point" class="wikilink">GM_Point</a> \</td\> \<td width="518"\>

The planimetric localization of the center of the cone of depression.\<br /\>The planimetric shape of a cone of depression os not necessarily circular. This discussion details size and shape characteristic of a cone of depression.\<br /\>The size and shape (slope) of the cone of depression depends on many factors. The pumping rate in the well will affect the size of the cone. Also, the type of aquifer material, such as whether the aquifer is gravel, sand, silt, fractured rocks, karst, etc., also will affect how far the cone extends. The amount of water in storage and the thickness of the aquifer also will determine the size and shape of the cone of depression. As a well is pumped, the cone of depression will extend out and will continue to expand in a radial fashion until a point of equilibrium occurs. This usually is when the amount of water released from storage equals the rate of pumping. This also can occur when recharge to the aquifer equals the amount of water being pumped. We typically think of a cone of depression as being a circular feature surrounding the pumped well. However, aquifer characteristics can affect the shape of the cone of depression. For example, if there is a steep ground-water gradient in the area of pumpage, the cone will tend to be shorter in the upgradient direction and elongated in the downgradient direction. This is because the water is already flowing towards the well from the upgradient direction, so the cone of depression doesn't need to extend as far out to obtain water, whereas the water is flowing away from the well in the downgradient direction, so the cone of depression needs to reach further to obtain water.\<br /\><http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cone_of_depression> \</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

\</td\> \<td width="56"\>

**depth** \</td\> \<td width="188"\>

<a href="QuantityValue" class="wikilink">QuantityValue</a> \</td\> \<td width="518"\>

The depth of a cone of depression in an aquifer. \</td\> \</tr\> \<tr\> \<td\>

N/A \</td\> \<td width="188"\>
